<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">International Workers' Day</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">This article is about International Workers' Day on 1 May, a holiday sometimes called May Day. See <a href="/wiki/May_Day" title="May Day">May Day</a> for the traditional spring holiday. See <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a> for other labour-related holidays.</div>

<p><b>International Workers' Day</b>, also known as <b>Labour Day</b> in some countries, is a celebration of <a href="/wiki/Wage_labour" title="Wage labour">labourers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working classes</a> that is promoted by the international <a href="/wiki/Labour_movement" title="Labour movement">labour movement</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist" title="Socialist">socialists</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist" title="Communist">communists</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchist" title="Anarchist">anarchists</a> and occurs every year on <a href="/wiki/May_Day" title="May Day">May Day</a> (1 May), an ancient European spring festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foner_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Foner-2">[2]</a></sup> The date was chosen for International Workers' Day by the <a href="/wiki/Second_International" title="Second International">Second International</a>, a pan-national organization of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist" title="Socialist">socialist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist" title="Communist">communist</a> political parties, to commemorate the <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_affair" title="Haymarket affair">Haymarket affair</a>, which occurred in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> on 4 May 1886.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foner_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Foner-2">[2]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Socialist_Congress,_Amsterdam_1904" title="International Socialist Congress, Amsterdam 1904">1904 International Socialist Conference</a> in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, the Sixth Conference of the Second International, called on "all Social Democratic Party organisations and trade unions of all countries to demonstrate energetically on the First of May for the legal establishment of the 8-hour day, for the class demands of the proletariat, and for universal peace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lunacharsky_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lunacharsky-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Being a traditional European spring celebration, May Day is a national <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">public holiday</a> in several European countries. The date is currently celebrated specifically as "Labour Day" or "International Workers' Day" in the majority of countries, including those which didn't traditionally celebrate May Day. Some countries celebrate a <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a> on other dates significant to them, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, which celebrates <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a> on the first Monday of September.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="1405" height="94" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day.svg/220px-Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day.svg/330px-Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day.svg/440px-Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
States and dependencies coloured by observance of International Workers' Day or a different variant of <a href="/wiki/May_Day" title="May Day">May Day</a> or <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a>:
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0080ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Labor holiday on or near 1 May</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #80b9ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Another public holiday on 1 May, such as <a href="/wiki/May_Day" title="May Day">May Day</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff8080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> No public holiday on 1 May, but <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a> on a different date</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> No public holiday on 1 May and no Labour Day</div>
</div>
</div>

<tr>
<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Socialism_sidebar" title="Template:Socialism sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Socialism_sidebar" title="Template talk:Socialism sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Socialism_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Beginning in the late 19th century, as the <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Labour_movement" title="Labour movement">labour movements</a> grew, a variety of days were chosen by trade unionists as a day to celebrate labour. In the United States and Canada, a September holiday, called <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor</a> or <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a>, was first proposed in the 1880s. In 1882, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Maguire_(labor_activist)" title="Matthew Maguire (labor activist)">Matthew Maguire</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Machinist" title="Machinist">machinist</a>, first proposed a Labor Day holiday on the first Monday of September<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[nb 1]</a></sup> while serving as secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Labor_Union" title="Central Labor Union">Central Labor Union</a> (CLU) of New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-labordept_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-labordept-4">[4]</a></sup> Others argue that it was first proposed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_J._McGuire" title="Peter J. McGuire">Peter J. McGuire</a> of the <a href="/wiki/American_Federation_of_Labor" title="American Federation of Labor">American Federation of Labor</a> in May 1882,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bridgemens1921_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bridgemens1921-6">[5]</a></sup> after witnessing the annual <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day#Canada_.28country.29" title="Labour Day">labour festival</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-origins_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-origins-7">[6]</a></sup> In 1887, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a> was the first state of the United States to make it an official <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">public holiday</a>. By the time it became an official <a href="/wiki/Federal_holiday" title="Federal holiday">federal holiday</a> in 1894, thirty <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. states</a> officially celebrated Labor Day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bridgemens1921_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bridgemens1921-6">[5]</a></sup> Thus by 1887 in North America, Labor Day was an established, official holiday but in September,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> not on 1 May.</p>
<p>1 May was chosen to be International Workers' Day in order to commemorate the 4 May 1886 <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_affair" title="Haymarket affair">Haymarket affair</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>. The police were trying to disperse a public assembly during a general strike for the <a href="/wiki/Eight-hour_day" title="Eight-hour day">eight-hour workday</a>, when an unidentified person threw a bomb at the police. The police responded by firing on the workers, killing four demonstrators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the_bomb_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-the_bomb-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[nb 2]</a></sup> The following day on 5 May in Milwaukee Wisconsin, the state militia fired on a crowd of strikers killing seven, including a schoolboy and a man feeding chickens in his yard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1889, a meeting in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> was held by the first congress of the <a href="/wiki/Second_International" title="Second International">Second International</a>, following a proposal by Raymond Lavigne which called for international demonstrations on the 1890 anniversary of the Chicago protests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foner_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Foner-2">[2]</a></sup> May Day was formally recognised as an annual event at the International's second congress in 1891.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Subsequently, the <a href="/wiki/May_Day_riots_of_1894" title="May Day riots of 1894">May Day riots of 1894</a> occurred. The <a href="/wiki/International_Socialist_Congress,_Amsterdam_1904" title="International Socialist Congress, Amsterdam 1904">International Socialist Congress, Amsterdam 1904</a> called on "all <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">Social Democratic</a> Party organisations and <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unions</a> of all countries to demonstrate energetically on the First of May for the legal establishment of the 8-hour day, for the class demands of the proletariat, and for universal peace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lunacharsky_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lunacharsky-3">[3]</a></sup> The congress made it "mandatory upon the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proletarian" title="Proletarian">proletarian</a> organisations of all countries to stop work on 1 May, wherever it is possible without injury to the workers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lunacharsky_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lunacharsky-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="982" data-file-width="1500" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg/220px-IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg/330px-IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg/440px-IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A 1 May rally in <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> in 1967</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>May Day has long been a focal point for <a href="/wiki/Demonstration_(protest)" title="Demonstration (protest)">demonstrations</a> by various socialist, communist and anarchist groups. May Day is one of the most important holidays in socialistic countries such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and the former <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. May Day celebrations in these countries typically feature elaborate military parades.</p>
<p>In 1955, the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> dedicated 1 May to "<a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph" title="Saint Joseph">Saint Joseph</a> the Worker". Saint Joseph is the <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> of workers and craftsmen, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saint_Joseph_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Saint_Joseph-13">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, May Day became the occasion for large military parades in <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and attended by the top leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Kremlin" title="Kremlin">Kremlin</a>, especially the <a href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Politburo of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Politburo</a>, atop <a href="/wiki/Lenin%27s_Mausoleum" title="Lenin's Mausoleum">Lenin's Mausoleum</a>. It became an enduring symbol of that period.</p>
<p>Today, the majority of countries around the world celebrate a workers' day on May 1.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Algeria">Algeria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Algeria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Algeria, 1 May is a public labour holiday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> 1 May is celebrated in Algeria as Labour Day and has been a paid <a href="/wiki/Bank_holiday" title="Bank holiday">bank holiday</a> since 1962.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Egyptian_Communist_Party_flags_in_Tahrir_Square.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="686" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Egyptian_Communist_Party_flags_in_Tahrir_Square.jpg/220px-Egyptian_Communist_Party_flags_in_Tahrir_Square.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Egyptian_Communist_Party_flags_in_Tahrir_Square.jpg/330px-Egyptian_Communist_Party_flags_in_Tahrir_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Egyptian_Communist_Party_flags_in_Tahrir_Square.jpg/440px-Egyptian_Communist_Party_flags_in_Tahrir_Square.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Egyptian_Communist_Party_flags_in_Tahrir_Square.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Egyptian Communist Party flags in <a href="/wiki/Tahrir_Square" title="Tahrir Square">Tahrir Square</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>1 May is known as Labour Day and is considered a paid holiday. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Egypt" title="President of Egypt">President of Egypt</a> traditionally presides over the official May Day celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ethiopia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, 1 May is a public holiday and celebrated as the Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kenya">Kenya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Kenya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, 1 May is a public holiday and celebrated as the Labour Day. It is a big day addressed by the leaders of the workers' umbrella union body - Central Organisation of Trade Unions COTU. The Minister for Labour (and occasionally the President) address the workers. Each year, the government approves (and increases) the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> on Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libya">Libya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Libya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>International Workers' Day was declared a national public holiday by the <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">National Transitional Council</a> in 2012 the first year of the post-Qaddafi era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 May 1978, then <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libyan</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Colonel Mu'ammar Al-Qaddafi</a> addressed the nation in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a> calling for <a href="/wiki/Administration_(law)" title="Administration (law)">administrative</a> and also <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economic</a> <a href="/wiki/History_of_Libya_under_Muammar_Gaddafi#Reforms_.281977.E2.80.931980.29" title="History of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi">reforms across Libya</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Morocco">Morocco</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Morocco">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It is recognised as a public holiday on 1 May.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nigeria">Nigeria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Nigeria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Every 1 May, workers in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> converge at the stadium to commemorate this public holiday. It is a recognised holiday which all workers have to observe. On that day the president of the <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_Labour_Congress" title="Nigeria Labour Congress">Nigeria Labour Congress</a> addresses workers and this has been a tradition for decades.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Day" title="Workers' Day">Workers' Day</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, Workers' Day has been celebrated as a national public holiday on 1 May each year since 1994.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tanzania">Tanzania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tanzania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, it is a public holiday on 1 May and celebrated as the Workers' Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tunisia">Tunisia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tunisia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1st_of_May_protest,_Tunis,_Tunisia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="1024" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg/220px-1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg/330px-1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg/440px-1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

May Day rally in <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>1 May is recognised as Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Zimbabwe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is recognised as Public Holiday in Zimbabwe. If the date is Sunday in that year, the following Monday will be a holiday.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="America">America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Argentina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, Workers' Day is an official holiday, and is frequently associated with the labour unions. Celebrations related to labour are held, including demonstrations in major cities. It is customary to organise meetings at friends' places, at the sports associations, at the workplace, or at the labour unions with local food, usually <a href="/wiki/Locro" title="Locro">locro</a> or <a href="/wiki/Asado" title="Asado">asado</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The first Workers' Day celebration was in 1890, when Argentinian unions, controlled in those days by socialists and anarchists, organised several joint celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a> and other cities, at the same time that the international labour movement celebrated it for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ElHistoriador_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-ElHistoriador-17">[15]</a></sup> In 1930, it was established as an official holiday by the first president elected after the passage of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A1enz_Pe%C3%B1a_Law" title="Sáenz Peña Law">Sáenz Peña Law</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Radical_Civic_Union" title="Radical Civic Union">Radical Civic Union</a> president <a href="/wiki/Hip%C3%B3lito_Yrigoyen" title="Hipólito Yrigoyen">Hipólito Yrigoyen</a>. The day became particularly relevant during the worker-oriented government of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juan_Domingo_Per%C3%B3n" title="Juan Domingo Perón">Juan Domingo Perón</a> (1946–55).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup> He permitted and endorsed national recognition of the holiday during his tenure in office.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bolivia">Bolivia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Bolivia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is known as Labour Day and is a holiday.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <b>Workers' Day</b> is an official holiday, and unions commemorate it with day-long public events. It is also when salaries for most professional categories and the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> are traditionally readjusted.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Journ%C3%A9e_internationale_des_travailleurs_et_travailleuses_anticapitaliste_-_Montr%C3%A9al.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Journ%C3%A9e_internationale_des_travailleurs_et_travailleuses_anticapitaliste_-_Montr%C3%A9al.jpg/220px-Journ%C3%A9e_internationale_des_travailleurs_et_travailleuses_anticapitaliste_-_Montr%C3%A9al.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Journ%C3%A9e_internationale_des_travailleurs_et_travailleuses_anticapitaliste_-_Montr%C3%A9al.jpg/330px-Journ%C3%A9e_internationale_des_travailleurs_et_travailleuses_anticapitaliste_-_Montr%C3%A9al.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Journ%C3%A9e_internationale_des_travailleurs_et_travailleuses_anticapitaliste_-_Montr%C3%A9al.jpg/440px-Journ%C3%A9e_internationale_des_travailleurs_et_travailleuses_anticapitaliste_-_Montr%C3%A9al.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Journ%C3%A9e_internationale_des_travailleurs_et_travailleuses_anticapitaliste_-_Montr%C3%A9al.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A notice about an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-capitalist" title="Anti-capitalist">anti-capitalist</a> rally on Worker's Day in Montreal, 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Canada, <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a> is celebrated in September. In 1894, the government of Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Sparrow_David_Thompson" title="John Sparrow David Thompson">John Sparrow David Thompson</a> declared the first Monday in September as Canada's official Labour Day. Labor Day in the United States is on the same day.</p>
<p>May Day is however marked by unions and leftists. May Day is an important day of trade union and community group protest in the province of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> (though not a provincial <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Canada" title="Public holidays in Canada">state holiday</a>). Celebration of the International Labour Day (or "International Workers' Day"; French translation: <i>Journée internationale des travailleurs</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> goes back to 1906, organised by the Mutual Aid circle. The tradition had a renaissance at the time of a mass strike in 1972. On the 1973 May Day, the first contemporary demonstration was organised by the major trade union confederations; over 30 000 trade unionists took part in this demonstration. Further, it is the customary date on which the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> rises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>President <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Ib%C3%A1%C3%B1ez_del_Campo" title="Carlos Ibáñez del Campo">Carlos Ibáñez del Campo</a> decreed 1 May a national holiday in 1931, in honour of the dignity of workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> All stores and public services must close for the entire day, and the major trade unions of Chile, represented in the national organisation <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_United_Center_of_Chile" title="Workers' United Center of Chile">Workers' United Center of Chile</a> (Central Unitaria de Trabajadores), organise rallies during the morning hours, with festivities and cookouts in the later part of the day, in all the major cities of Chile. During these rallies, representatives of the major left-wing political parties speak to the assemblies on the issues of the day concerning workers’ rights.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">Colombia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Colombia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May has long been recognised as Labour Day and almost all workers respect it as a national holiday. As in many other countries, it is common to see rallies by the trade unions in all over the main regional capitals of the country.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Costa_Rica">Costa Rica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Costa Rica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It is recognised as a public holiday, and at the same time an important day for government activities. On this day the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_of_Costa_Rica" title="President of Costa Rica">President of Costa Rica</a> gives a speech to the citizens and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislature_of_Costa_Rica" title="Legislature of Costa Rica">legislature of Costa Rica</a> about the duties that were undertaken through the previous year. The president of the legislature is also chosen by its members.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This day is known as Labour Day in Cuba. People march in the streets, showing their support to the Cuban Communist government and the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> during the whole morning.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominican_Republic">Dominican Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Dominican Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is a national holiday known as Labour Day which is celebrated by workers' parades and demonstration.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecuador">Ecuador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ecuador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It is recognised as a public holiday known as Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="El_Salvador">El Salvador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: El Salvador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It is an official holiday and it is commemorated with parades.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guatemala">Guatemala</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Guatemala">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is an official public holiday known as Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Haiti">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is an official public holiday known as Agriculture and Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is a federal holiday known as Labour Day. It also commemorates the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cananea_Strike" title="Cananea Strike">Cananea Strike</a> of 1906 in the Mexican state of <a href="/wiki/Sonora" title="Sonora">Sonora</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Panama">Panama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Panama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is an official public holiday known as Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paraguay">Paraguay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Paraguay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is an official public holiday known as Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peru">Peru</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Peru">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is an official public holiday known as Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Socialists_in_Union_Square,_N.Y.C..jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4260" data-file-width="5779" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg/220px-Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg/330px-Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg/440px-Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Socialists_in_Union_Square,_N.Y.C..jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Socialists in Union Square, N.Y.C. on 1 May 1912</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the United States, efforts to switch Labor Day from September to 1 May have not been successful. In 1921, following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1917" title="Russian Revolution of 1917">Russian Revolution of 1917</a>, 1 May was promoted as "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Americanization_Day" title="Americanization Day">Americanization Day</a>" by the <a href="/wiki/Veterans_of_Foreign_Wars" title="Veterans of Foreign Wars">Veterans of Foreign Wars</a> and other groups in <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">opposition to communism</a>. It became an annual event, sometimes featuring large rallies. In 1949, Americanization Day was renamed to <a href="/wiki/Loyalty_Day" title="Loyalty Day">Loyalty Day</a>. In 1958, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress">U.S. Congress</a> declared Loyalty Day, the U.S. recognition of 1 May, a national holiday; that same year, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> proclaimed 1 May <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Law_Day" title="Law Day">Law Day</a> as well.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Commemoration_to_the_fallen_in_Milwaukee_WI.jpg"><img alt="Milwaukee May Day Commemoration" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="508" data-file-width="800" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Commemoration_to_the_fallen_in_Milwaukee_WI.jpg/220px-Commemoration_to_the_fallen_in_Milwaukee_WI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Commemoration_to_the_fallen_in_Milwaukee_WI.jpg/330px-Commemoration_to_the_fallen_in_Milwaukee_WI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Commemoration_to_the_fallen_in_Milwaukee_WI.jpg/440px-Commemoration_to_the_fallen_in_Milwaukee_WI.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Commemoration_to_the_fallen_in_Milwaukee_WI.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Music, theatre and giant puppets mark the Milwaukee May Day commemoration.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Unions and union locals in the United States — especially in urban areas with strong support for organised labour — have maintained a connection with labour traditions through their own unofficial observances on 1 May. Some of the largest examples of this occurred during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> of the 1930s, when hundreds of thousands of workers marched in May Day <a href="/wiki/Parade" title="Parade">parades</a> in New York's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Square_(New_York_City)" title="Union Square (New York City)">Union Square</a>. <a href="/wiki/Political_radicalism" title="Political radicalism">Radical</a> organisations including <a href="/wiki/American_Left" title="American Left">anarchist groups and socialist and communist parties</a> have kept the May Day tradition alive with rallies and demonstrations in such cities as New York, Chicago and Seattle, often with major union backing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> In Milwaukee, an annual commemoration takes place at the site of the killing of seven workers during an 8 hour march.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">[10]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg/220px-San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg/330px-San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg/440px-San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a>, May Day March, 1 May 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2006, 1 May was chosen by mostly <a href="/wiki/Latino" title="Latino">Latino</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrant" title="Immigrant">immigrant</a> groups in the United States as the day for the <a href="/wiki/Great_American_Boycott" title="Great American Boycott">Great American Boycott</a>, a <a href="/wiki/General_strike" title="General strike">general strike</a> of undocumented immigrant workers and supporters to protest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Border_Protection,_Anti-terrorism,_and_Illegal_Immigration_Control_Act_of_2005" title="Border Protection, Anti-terrorism, and Illegal Immigration Control Act of 2005">H.R. 4437</a>, immigration reform legislation which they felt was draconian. From 10 April to 1 May of that year, millions of immigrant families in the U.S. called for immigrant rights, workers' rights and amnesty for undocumented workers. They were joined by socialist and other leftist organisations on 1 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> On 1 May 2007, a mostly peaceful demonstration in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> in support of undocumented immigrant workers ended with a widely televised <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_May_Day_m%C3%AAl%C3%A9e" title="Los Angeles May Day mêlée">dispersal by police officers</a>. In March 2008, the <a href="/wiki/International_Longshore_and_Warehouse_Union" title="International Longshore and Warehouse Union">International Longshore and Warehouse Union</a> announced that <a href="/wiki/Stevedore" title="Stevedore">dockworkers</a> will move no <a href="/wiki/Cargo" title="Cargo">cargo</a> at any <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">West Coast</a> ports on 1 May 2008, as a protest against the continuation of the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> and the diversion of resources from domestic needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> For May Day 2010, marches were being planned in many cities uniting immigrant and native workers including New York,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> San Francisco,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> Boston,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> Albany<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> Chicago and Los Angeles most of whom protested against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arizona_Senate_Bill_1070" title="Arizona Senate Bill 1070">Arizona Senate Bill 1070</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 May 2012, members of <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy Wall Street</a> and labour unions held protests together in a number of cities in the United States and Canada to commemorate May Day and to protest the state of the economy and economic inequality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uruguay">Uruguay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Uruguay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Uruguay, 1 May – Workers' Day – is an official holiday. Even when it is associated with labour unions, almost all workers tend to respect it. Since the late 1990s, the main event takes place at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=First_of_May_Square,_Montevideo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="First of May Square, Montevideo (page does not exist)">First of May Square</a> in Montevideo.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is an official holiday in Venezuela. <span lang="es" xml:lang="es"><i>El Día del Trabajador</i></span> is celebrated on 1 May in Venezuela since 1936, but from 1938 to 1945 it was held on 24 July, by an order of <a href="/wiki/Eleazar_L%C3%B3pez_Contreras" title="Eleazar López Contreras">Eleazar López Contreras</a>. However, <a href="/wiki/Isa%C3%ADas_Medina_Angarita" title="Isaías Medina Angarita">Isaías Medina Angarita</a> changed it back to 1 May in 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bahrain">Bahrain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Bahrain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Bahrain, 1 May is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Bangladesh, May Day is a government holiday. All labor oriented organizations celebrate the day with great honor and dignity. Schools and colleges under government jurisdictions enjoy holiday on this day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cambodia">Cambodia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Cambodia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Cambodia, it is known as International Labour Day and is a public holiday.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:8500_Prociss%C3%A3o_em_Macau_em_1_de_Maio_de_2010.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/8500_Prociss%C3%A3o_em_Macau_em_1_de_Maio_de_2010.JPG/220px-8500_Prociss%C3%A3o_em_Macau_em_1_de_Maio_de_2010.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/8500_Prociss%C3%A3o_em_Macau_em_1_de_Maio_de_2010.JPG/330px-8500_Prociss%C3%A3o_em_Macau_em_1_de_Maio_de_2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/8500_Prociss%C3%A3o_em_Macau_em_1_de_Maio_de_2010.JPG/440px-8500_Prociss%C3%A3o_em_Macau_em_1_de_Maio_de_2010.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:8500_Prociss%C3%A3o_em_Macau_em_1_de_Maio_de_2010.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Protest march in <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, China, 1 May 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>1 May is a statutory holiday in the People's Republic of China. Prior to 2008, it was a three-day holiday, but is now just the one day. However, it is usually supplemented by two other days to give the appearance of a three-day holiday, but not being statutory holidays the extra days have to be "made up" by working either the preceding or following weekend. For example, in 2013, 1 May fell on Wednesday. Most workplaces, including all government offices, took Monday 29 April, Tuesday 30 April, and Wednesday 1 May off. As the first two days are not statutory holidays they have to be "made up" by working the preceding weekend (27 and 28 April). In Hong Kong,1 May is known as Labour Day and has been considered a public holiday since 1999.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Georgia">Georgia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Georgia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, because of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet" title="Soviet">Soviet</a> past, lists 1 May as a public holiday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg/220px-Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg/330px-Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg/440px-Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Triumph_of_Labour" title="Triumph of Labour">Triumph of Labour</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Marina_Beach" title="Marina Beach">Marina Beach</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In India, Labour Day is a public holiday held on every 1 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> It is celebrated as <b>Antarrashtriya Shramik Diwas</b>. The holiday is tied to labour movements for communist and socialist political parties. Labour Day is known as "Kamgar Din" in <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, "Kamgar Divas" in Marathi and "Uzhaipalar dhinam" in Tamil. In <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">North India</a>, Labour Day is mostly not given its previous importance as a holiday now.</p>
<p>The first May Day celebration in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> was organised in Madras (now <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>) by the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Kisan_Party_of_Hindustan" title="Labour Kisan Party of Hindustan">Labour Kisan Party of Hindustan</a> on 1 May 1923.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> This was also the first time the <a href="/wiki/Red_flag_(politics)" title="Red flag (politics)">red flag</a> was used in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rao1_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-rao1-39">[37]</a></sup> The party leader <a href="/wiki/Malayapuram_Singaravelu_Chettiar" title="Malayapuram Singaravelu Chettiar">Singaravelu Chettiar</a> made arrangements to celebrate May Day in two places in 1923. One meeting was held at the beach opposite to the <a href="/wiki/Madras_High_Court" title="Madras High Court">Madras High Court</a>; the other meeting was held at the <a href="/wiki/Triplicane" title="Triplicane">Triplicane</a> beach. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a></i> newspaper, published from Madras reported,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>The Labour Kisan party has introduced May Day celebrations in Madras. Comrade Singaravelar presided over the meeting. A resolution was passed stating that the government should declare May Day as a holiday. The president of the party explained the non-violent principles of the party. There was a request for financial aid. It was emphasised that workers of the world must unite to achieve independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>1 May is also celebrated as "<a href="/wiki/Maharashtra_Day" title="Maharashtra Day">Maharashtra Day</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gujarat_Day" title="Gujarat Day">Gujarat Day</a>" to mark the date in 1960, when the two western states attained statehood after the erstwhile <a href="/wiki/Bombay_State" title="Bombay State">Bombay State</a> was divided on linguistic lines. Maharashtra Day is held at <a href="/wiki/Shivaji" title="Shivaji">Shivaji</a> Park in central <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>. Schools and offices in Maharashtra remain closed on 1 May. A similar parade is held to celebrate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gujarat_Day" title="Gujarat Day">Gujarat Day</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gandhinagar" title="Gandhinagar">Gandhinagar</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Protest_march_in_Jakarta,_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="461" data-file-width="614" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg/220px-Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg/330px-Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg/440px-Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Protest_march_in_Jakarta,_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Protest march in Jakarta, Indonesia, 1 May 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>May Day (often referred locally as Labour Day) in Indonesia was first observed as a public holiday from 2014. Every year on the day, labourers take over the streets in major cities across the country, voicing their demands for better income &amp; a supportive policy by the ministries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Iran, 1 May is known as the International Workers' Day. It is not a public holiday but according to article 63 of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranian_labour_law" title="Iranian labour law">Iranian labour law</a> on top of the official public holidays observed in the Islamic Republic of Iran, Labour Day shall be considered an official holiday for workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iraq">Iraq</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Iraq">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Iraq, it is known as the International Workers' Day and is a public holiday.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="700" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG/220px-PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG/330px-PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG/440px-PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Israel, 1 May 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Israel" title="State of Israel">State of Israel</a>, 1 May is not an official holiday. <a href="/wiki/Avodah" title="Avodah">Avodah</a>-affiliated organisations and the <a href="/wiki/Histadrut" title="Histadrut">Histadrut</a> recognise this international holiday.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="266" data-file-width="400" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg/220px-NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg/330px-NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/35/NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2011 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zenrokyo" title="Zenrokyo">National Trade Union Council (<i>Zenrokyo</i>)</a> May Day march, Tokyo.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>May Day is not officially designated by the Japanese government as a national holiday, but as it lies between other national holidays, it is a day off work for the vast majority of Japanese workers. Many employers give it as a day off, and otherwise workers take it as "paid leave". 1 May occurs during "<a href="/wiki/Golden_Week_(Japan)" title="Golden Week (Japan)">Golden Week</a>", together with 29 April ("<a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Dwa_Day" title="Shōwa Day">Shōwa Day</a>"), 3 May ("<a href="/wiki/Constitution_Memorial_Day" title="Constitution Memorial Day">Constitution Memorial Day</a>"), 4 May ("<a href="/wiki/Greenery_Day" title="Greenery Day">Greenery Day</a>") and 5 May ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kodomo_no_hi" title="Kodomo no hi">Children's Day</a>"). Workers generally take the day off work not so much to join street rallies or labour union gatherings, but more to go on holiday for several consecutive days (in Japanese corporate culture, taking weekdays off for personal pleasure is widely frowned upon).</p>
<p>Some major labour unions organise rallies and demonstrations in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nagoya" title="Nagoya">Nagoya</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Japan has a long history of labour activism and since 1945, has had a communist and socialist party in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Diet" title="Japanese Diet">Diet</a>. In 2008, the National Confederation of Trade Unions (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zenr%C5%8Dren&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zenrōren (page does not exist)">Zenrōren</a></i>) held a rally in <a href="/wiki/Yoyogi_Park" title="Yoyogi Park">Yoyogi Park</a> attended by 44,000 participants, while the National Trade Unions Council (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zenrokyo" title="Zenrokyo">Zenrōkyō</a></i>) held its May Day rally at <a href="/wiki/Hibiya_Park" title="Hibiya Park">Hibiya Park</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <i><a href="/wiki/RENGO" title="RENGO">Rengō</a></i>, the largest Japanese trade union, held its May Day rally on the following Saturday (3 May), allegedly to distance itself from the more radical labour unions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jordan">Jordan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Jordan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lebanon">Lebanon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Lebanon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is known as the Workers' Day and is a public holiday. From the 1960s through the 1990s, left-wing parties and workers' unions organised major marches on this day. Recently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2013)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup>, only symbolic marches take place on this day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Macau">Macau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Macau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is officially known as <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt"><i>Dia do Trabalhador</i></span> in Portuguese. It is a public holiday in this <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Administrative_Region_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Special Administrative Region of the People's Republic of China">Special Administrative Region of the People's Republic of China</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> began observing the holiday in 1972 following an announcement by the late <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_Malaysia" title="Deputy Prime Minister of Malaysia">Malaysian Deputy Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Abdul_Rahman" title="Ismail Abdul Rahman">Ismail Abdul Rahman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maldives">Maldives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Maldives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> first observed the holiday in 2011, after a declaration by <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Maldives" title="President of the Maldives">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Nasheed" title="Mohamed Nasheed">Mohamed Nasheed</a>. He noted that this move highlighted the government’s commitment as well as efforts of private parties to protect and promote workers’ rights in the Maldives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Myanmar">Myanmar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Myanmar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Myanmar, 1 May is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nepal">Nepal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Nepal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>May Day has been celebrated in <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> since 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> The day became a public holiday in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Korea">North Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: North Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_People%27s_Republic_of_Korea" title="Democratic People's Republic of Korea">Democratic People's Republic of Korea</a>, 1 May is known as International Workers' Day, and is a public holiday. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rungnado_May_Day_Stadium" title="Rungnado May Day Stadium">Rungnado May Day Stadium</a> in the capital of <a href="/wiki/Pyongyang" title="Pyongyang">Pyongyang</a> was built in honour of the holiday.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>International Labour Day is observed in Pakistan on 1 May to commemorate the social and economic achievements of workers. It is a public and national holiday. All government and non-government organisations, factories and educational institutions remain closed on this day. Currently (2015), it is honoured by every single organisation in Pakistan to give respect to all those who worked, to those who are working and those who played a part in social as well as economic conditions.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Palestine">Palestine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Palestine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is known as <b>Labor Day</b> (<i>Araw ng mga Manggaggawa</i>) and is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_holiday_in_the_Philippines" title="Public holiday in the Philippines">public holiday in the Philippines</a>. On this day, labour organisations and unions hold protests in major cities. On 1 May 1903, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Colonial_Period_of_the_Philippines" title="American Colonial Period of the Philippines">American colonial period</a> the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Obrera_Democratica_Filipina" title="Union Obrera Democratica Filipina">Union Obrera Democratica Filipina</a></i> (Filipino Democratic Labor Union) held a 100,000-person<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InquirerLaborDay_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-InquirerLaborDay-48">[46]</a></sup> rally in front of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1an_Palace" title="Malacañan Palace">Malacañan Palace</a> demanding workers' economic rights and Philippine independence.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Ten years later, the first official<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (December 2013)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> celebration was held on 1 May 1913 when 36 labour unions convened for a congress in <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InquirerLaborDay_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-InquirerLaborDay-48">[46]</a></sup> On 1 May 2001, a mass demonstration occurred near <a href="/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace" title="Malacañang Palace">Malacañang Palace</a> known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EDSA_3#May_1" title="EDSA 3">EDSA 3</a> or 1 May Riots.</p>
<p>During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo" title="Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo">Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo</a>, a policy was adopted called <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_Philippines#.22Holiday_Economics.22" title="Public holidays in the Philippines">holiday economics</a> policy that moved holidays to either a Monday or a Friday to create a <a href="/wiki/Long_weekend" title="Long weekend">long weekend</a> of three days. In 2002, Labor Day was moved to the Monday nearest to 1 May. Labour groups protested, as they accused the Arroyo administration of belittling the holiday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> By 2008, Labor Day was excluded in the holiday economics policy, returning the commemorations to 1 May, no matter what day of the week it falls on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Singapore, it is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Korea">South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: South Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Korea" title="Republic of Korea">Republic of Korea</a>, 1 May is known simply as "Workers' Day". It is not a public holiday, but a paid holiday for workers by the <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/ko:%EB%8C%80%ED%95%9C%EB%AF%BC%EA%B5%AD_%EA%B7%BC%EB%A1%9C%EC%9E%90%EC%9D%98%EB%82%A0%EC%A0%9C%EC%A0%95%EC%97%90%EA%B4%80%ED%95%9C%EB%B2%95%EB%A5%A0" title="s:ko:대한민국 근로자의날제정에관한법률">Designation of Workers' Day Act</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[nb 3]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sri_Lanka">Sri Lanka</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Sri Lanka">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Sri Lanka, it is observed on 1 May and is a government and public holiday. The government has held official May Day celebrations in major towns and cities, with the largest being in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a>. During celebrations, it is common to witness party leaders greeting the crowds. Workers frequently carry banners with political slogans and many parties decorate their vehicles.</p>
