<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syria">Syria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Syria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 May is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (Taiwan's official name), 1 May is an official public holiday known as Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Thailand, the day is known in English as National Labour Day, and is one of 16 official <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Thailand" title="Public holidays in Thailand">public holidays in Thailand</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam">Vietnam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Vietnam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Vietnam, it is known as International Labour Day and is a public holiday. The word International Workers' Day in Vietnamese is <b>Ngày Quốc tế Lao động</b>. It was first celebrated in 1913.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Bloc_under_communist_governments">Eastern Bloc under communist governments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Eastern Bloc under communist governments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="598" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg/170px-RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg/255px-RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg/340px-RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May Day rally in Moscow, 1 May 1960</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> countries such as the Soviet Union and most countries of central and eastern Europe that were under the rule of communist governments held official May Day celebrations in every town and city, during which party leaders greeted the crowds. Workers carried banners with political slogans and many companies decorated their company cars. The biggest celebration of 1 May usually occurred in the capital of a particular communist country and usually included a military display and the presence of the president and the secretary general of the party. In <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, since 1982, party leaders led the official parades, and in 1990, 1 May was renamed "State Holiday." In Hungary, May Day was officially celebrated under the communist regime, and remains a public holiday. Traditionally, the day was marked by dancing around designated "May trees."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> Some factories in communist countries were named in honour of International Workers' Day, such as <a href="/wiki/1_Maja_Coal_Mine" title="1 Maja Coal Mine">1 Maja Coal Mine</a> in Wodzisław Śląski, Poland.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Albania">Albania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Albania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Labour Day (<i>Dita e punëtorëve</i>) is an official holiday celebrated on 1 May.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Austria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Labour Day (<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Tag der Arbeit</span></i>), officially called <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Staatsfeiertag</span></i> (state's holiday), is a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Austria" title="Public holidays in Austria">public holiday in Austria</a>. Left parties, especially social democrats organise celebrations with marches and speeches in all major cities. In smaller towns and villages those marches are held the night before.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgium">Belgium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Belgium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Belgium, Labour Day (Dutch: <i><span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl">Dag van de Arbeid</span></i>, <i><span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl">Feest van de Arbeid</span></i>, French: <i><span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">Journée des Travailleurs</span></i>, <i><span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">Fête du Travail</span></i>), is observed on 1 May and is an <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Belgium" title="Public holidays in Belgium">official holiday</a>. Various socialist and communist organisations hold parades in different cities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bosnia_and_Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Bosnia and Herzegovina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Bosnia and Herzegovina, 1 May (Bosnian and Serbian: <i>Prvi Maj</i>/Први Mај, Croatian: <i>Prvi Svibanj</i>) is an official holiday at the national level. Most people celebrate this holiday by visiting natural parks and resorts. Additionally, in some places public events are organised.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Bulgaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Labour Day is one of the <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Bulgaria" title="Public holidays in Bulgaria">public holidays in Bulgaria</a>, where it is known as <i>Labour Day and International Workers' Solidarity Day</i> (Ден на труда и на международната работническа солидарност). The first attempt to celebrate it was in 1890 by the Bulgarian Typographical Association. In 1939, Labour Day was declared an official holiday. Since 1945 the communist authorities in the People's Republic of Bulgaria began to celebrate the holiday every year. After the end of socialism in Bulgaria in 1989 Labour Day continues to be an official and public holiday, but state authorities are not committed to the organisation of mass events. It is celebrated annually on 1 May.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Croatia">Croatia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Croatia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Croatia, 1 May is a national holiday. People celebrate all over the country by gathering and cooking or barbecuing toghter. In <a href="/wiki/Zagreb" title="Zagreb">Zagreb</a>, the capital, most people go to <a href="/wiki/Maksimir_Park" title="Maksimir Park">Maksimir Park</a>, which is located in the east part of Zagreb. In Split, the largest city on the coast, people go to Marjan, a park-forest at the western end of Split peninsula. Many public events are organised and held all over the country where military style bean soup is given out to all people as a symbol of a real workers' dish.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Czech_Republic">Czech Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Czech Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the Czech Republic, 1 May is an official and national holiday known as Labour Day (<i>Svátek práce</i> in <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, 1 May is not an official holiday, but many people, mostly in the public sector, get a half or a whole day off. The day is celebrated in the biggest cities with speeches from politicians, labour market organisations, grass roots, etc.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Finland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="543" data-file-width="735" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg/220px-Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg/330px-Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg/440px-Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A May Day rally in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, Finland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Finland, 1 May is an official and national holiday. Apart from Workers' Day (officially: <i>suomalaisen työn päivä</i>, "day of Finnish labour"), it is also celebrated as a feast of students, and spring, called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vappu" title="Vappu">vappu</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wpi_france.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Wpi_france.jpg/220px-Wpi_france.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Wpi_france.jpg/330px-Wpi_france.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Wpi_france.jpg/440px-Wpi_france.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wpi_france.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May Day demonstration in <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, France</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In France, 1 May is a public holiday. It is, in fact, the only day of the year on which employees are legally obliged to be given leave, save professions which cannot be interrupted due to their nature (such as workers in hospitals and public transport).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup> Demonstrations and marches are a Labour Day tradition in France, where trade unions organise parades in major cities to defend workers' rights. It is also customary to offer a <a href="/wiki/Lily_of_the_valley" title="Lily of the valley">lily of the valley</a> to friends or family. This custom dates back to 1561, where <a href="/wiki/Charles_IX_of_France" title="Charles IX of France">Charles IX</a>, aged 10, waiting for his accession to the throne, gave a lily of the valley to all ladies present. Today, the fiscal administration exempts individuals and workers' organisations from any tax or administrative duties related to the sales of lilies of the valley, provided they are gathered from the wild, and not bought to be resold.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 1933, the recently installed <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi government</a> declared 1 May the "Day of National Work," an official state holiday, and announced that all celebrations were to be organised by the government. Any separate celebrations by communists, social democrats or <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">labour unions</a> were banned. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, 1 May remained a state holiday in both <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>. In communist East Germany, workers were <i>de facto</i> required to participate in large state-organised parades on May Day. Today in Germany it is simply called "Labour Day" (<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Tag der Arbeit</span></i>), and there are numerous demonstrations and celebrations by independent workers' organisations. Today, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> witnesses yearly demonstrations on May Day, the largest organised by labour unions, political parties and others by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far_left" title="Far left">far left</a> and <a href="/wiki/Autonomism" title="Autonomism">Autonomen</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_(168).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg/220px-1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg/330px-1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg/440px-1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_(168).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May Day rally in <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a>, Germany, 1 May 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 1987, May Day has also become known for riots in some districts of Berlin. After police actions against radical leftists in that year's annual demonstrations, the Autonome scattered and sought cover at the ongoing annual street fair in <a href="/wiki/Kreuzberg" title="Kreuzberg">Kreuzberg</a>. Three years prior to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reunification_of_Germany" title="Reunification of Germany">reunification of Germany</a>, violent protests would only take place in the former <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a>. The protesters began tipping over police cars, violently resisting arrest, and began building <a href="/wiki/Barricade" title="Barricade">barricades</a> after the police withdrew due to the unforeseen resistance. Cars were set on fire, shops plundered and burned to the ground. The police eventually ended the riots the following night. These violent forms of protests by the radical left, later increasingly involved participants without political motivation. (Read more: <a href="/wiki/May_Day_in_Kreuzberg" title="May Day in Kreuzberg">May Day in Kreuzberg</a>)</p>
<p>Annual street fairs have proven an effective way to prevent riots, and May Day in 2005 and 2006 have been among the most peaceful known to Berlin in nearly 25 years. In recent years, <a href="/wiki/Neo-Nazism" title="Neo-Nazism">neo-Nazis</a> and other groups on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far_right" title="Far right">far right</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="National Democratic Party of Germany">National Democratic Party of Germany</a>, have used the day to schedule public demonstrations, often leading to clashes with left-wing protesters, which turned especially violent in <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a> in 1998 and 2005.</p>
<p>May Day violence flared again in 2010. After an approved far right demonstration was blocked by leftists, a parade by an estimated 10,000 leftists and anarchists turned violent and resulted in an active response by Berlin police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Greece 1 May is an optional public holiday. The Ministry of Labour retains the right to classify it as an official public holiday on an annual basis, and it customarily does so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup> The day is called <i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Greek transliteration">Ergatikí Proto-magiá</span></i> (<span lang="el" xml:lang="el">Εργατική Πρωτομαγιά</span>, <abbr title="literally">lit.</abbr> "Workers' 1 May") and celebrations are marked by demonstrations in which left-wing political parties, anti-authority groups and workers' unions participate. On May Day 2010 there were major protests all over Greece, most notably Athens and <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, by many left, anarchist and communist supporters and some violent clashes with <a href="/wiki/Riot_police" title="Riot police">riot police</a> who were sent out to contain the protesters. They opposed economic reforms, an end to job losses and wage cuts in the face of the government's proposals of massive public spending cuts. These reforms are to fall in line with the IMF-EU-ECB loan proposals which demand that Greece liberalise its economy and cut its public spending and private sector wages, which many believe will decrease living standards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hungary celebrates 1 May as a national holiday, with open-air festivities and fairs all over the country. Many towns raise May poles and festivals with various themes are organised around the holiday. As with other holidays, whenever 1 May falls on a Tuesday or Thursday the holiday officially becomes a long weekend when families take off to travel and hotels are booked full. Left-wing parties continue to hold public rallies commemorating Labour Day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iceland">Iceland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: Iceland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Iceland the Labour Day (<i>Baráttudagur verkalýðsins</i>) is a public holiday. However many stores nowadays are open and pay higher salaries to the workers instead on this day. A parade composed of trade unions and other groups marches through towns and cities across the country and speeches are delivered.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>May Day celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">north</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">south</a>, are organised by the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Congress_of_Trade_Unions" title="Irish Congress of Trade Unions">Irish Congress of Trade Unions</a>. Rallies take place in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> and other events such as lectures, concerts and film screenings also take place around a wider May Day festival. Since 1994 a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Public holidays in the Republic of Ireland">public holiday in Ireland</a> is observed on the first Monday in May.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg/220px-Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg/330px-Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg/440px-Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Traditional 1st May Concert in St. John Lateran square, <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first May Day celebration in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> took place in 1890. It started initially as an attempt to celebrate workers' achievements in their struggle for their rights and for better social and economic conditions. It was abolished under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(1861%E2%80%931946)" title="Kingdom of Italy (1861–1946)">Fascist Regime</a> and immediately restored after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. (During the fascist period, a "Holiday of the Italian Labour" (<i>Festa del lavoro italiano</i>) was celebrated on 21 April, the date of <i>Natale di Roma</i>, when ancient <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> was allegedly founded.) May Day is now an important celebration in Italy and is a national holiday regardless of what day of the week it falls. The <i>Concerto del Primo Maggio</i> ("1st of May Concert"), organised by Italian labour unions in Rome in <a href="/wiki/Porta_San_Giovanni_(Rome)" title="Porta San Giovanni (Rome)">Piazza di Porta San Giovanni</a> has become an important event in recent years. Every year the concert is attended by a large audience of mostly young people and involves participation of many famous bands and songwriters, lasting from 3 p.m. till midnight. The concert is usually broadcast live by <a href="/wiki/Rai_3" title="Rai 3">Rai 3</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lithuania">Lithuania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Lithuania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>First May Day is an official public holiday celebrated as International Work Day (Tarptautinė darbo diena). First official celebrations appeared during <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states" title="Occupation of the Baltic states">Soviet occupation</a>, but it had negative communist connotation. As Lithuania declared its <a href="/wiki/Act_of_the_Re-Establishment_of_the_State_of_Lithuania" title="Act of the Re-Establishment of the State of Lithuania">independence</a> in 1990, Work Day lost its public holiday status, but regained it in 1996.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title="Edit section: Luxembourg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Luxembourg, 1 May, called the <i>Dag vun der Aarbecht</i> ("Day of Labour"), is a legal holiday traditionally associated with large demonstrations by trade unions in Luxembourg City and other cities. Many people seize the opportunity for an outdoor picnic with family and friends, and local and national associations organise popular events for this day, among others the Festival of Labour and Cultures, organised by the <a class="external text" href="https://www.neimenster.lu" rel="nofollow">Neumünster Abbey Cultural Exchange Centre</a> in Luxembourg City.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Macedonia">Macedonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=85" title="Edit section: Macedonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Macedonia, 1 May (Macedonian: Ден на Трудот) is an official public holiday. People celebrate with friends and family at traditional picnics across the country, accompanied by the usual outdoor games, various grilled meats and beverages.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malta">Malta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=86" title="Edit section: Malta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Malta, 1 May is an official public holiday celebrated as Workers' Day together with the religious feast of St. Joseph (Patron of Workers). A free music event also takes place on this date. The Maltese also celebrate the membership of Malta in the European Union of 2004.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=87" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="333" data-file-width="500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg/220px-Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg/330px-Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg/440px-Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Norway's former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jens_Stoltenberg" title="Jens Stoltenberg">Jens Stoltenberg</a> gives his 1 May speech in 2009 in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, Norway</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the Netherlands, 1 May is not an official holiday. However, several left-wing political parties and organisations celebrate International Workers' Day yearly. Small demonstrations are sometimes held, mostly by anarchist and radical socialist groups. One of the reasons labour day never got established as a national holiday might have been the fact that the day that used to immediately precede it, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koninginnedag" title="Koninginnedag">Queen's Day</a> (now King's Day at 27 April), was already a public holiday in its own right.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norway">Norway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=88" title="Edit section: Norway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Norway, Labour Day (<i>Arbeidernes Dag</i>) is celebrated May 1 and is an official public holiday. It is traditionally a day of marches, speeched and parties organized by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labour_union" title="Labour union">labour unions</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leftist" title="Leftist">leftist</a> <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political parties</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feminist" title="Feminist">feminist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-racist" title="Anti-racist">anti-racist</a> organizations in order to voice political concerns and to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Solidarity" title="Solidarity">solidarity</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=89" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG/220px-Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG/330px-Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG/440px-Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/1_Maja_Coal_Mine" title="1 Maja Coal Mine">1st May Coal Mine</a> in Wodzisław Śląski, Poland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Poland, since the fall of communism, 1 May is officially celebrated as <a href="/wiki/May_Day" title="May Day">May Day</a>, but is commonly called <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Poland" title="Public holidays in Poland">Labour Day</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup> It is currently celebrated without a specific connotation, and as such it is May Day. However, due to historical connotations, most of the celebrations are focused around Labour Day festivities. It is customary for labour activists to organize parades in cities and towns across Poland. The holiday is also commonly referred to as "Labour Day" ("Święto Pracy").</p>
<p>In Poland, May Day is closely followed by <a href="/wiki/May_3rd_Constitution_Day" title="May 3rd Constitution Day">May 3rd Constitution Day</a>. These two dates combined often result in a long weekend called "Majówka". People often travel, and "Majówka" is unofficially considered the start of barbecuing season in Poland. Between these two, on 2 May, there is a patriotic holiday, the Day of Polish Flag (<a class="extiw" href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dzie%C5%84_Flagi_Rzeczypospolitej_Polskiej" title="pl:Dzień Flagi Rzeczypospolitej Polskiej">Dzień Flagi Rzeczypospolitej Polskiej</a>), introduced by a Parliamentary Act of 20 February 2004.</p>
<p>In Poland some streets, places, squares, parks and also factories were popular named in honour of International Workers' Day, such as <a href="/wiki/1_Maja_Coal_Mine" title="1 Maja Coal Mine">1 Maja Coal Mine</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wodzis%C5%82aw_%C5%9Al%C4%85ski" title="Wodzisław Śląski">Wodzisław Śląski</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portugal">Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=90" title="Edit section: Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Portugal, the 1 May celebration ("Primeiro de Maio") was harshly repressed<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>during the long right wing dictatorship of <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Oliveira_Salazar" title="António de Oliveira Salazar">António de Oliveira Salazar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Caetano" title="Marcelo Caetano">Marcelo Caetano</a>. Since the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> on 25 April 1974, the Worker's Day is celebrated by unions but as well by several leftist political parties with parades and demonstrations. The first demonstration after the Carnation Revolution, only one week after the coup, stays until today as the biggest demonstration in the history of Portugal. It is an opportunity for workers, including non-permanent workers' groups, to show their discontent for existing working conditions in parades all over the country but mainly in the capital, where the two main national union federations (communist CGTP-IN and centre-left UGT) organise two different rallies (in Alameda D. Afonso Henriques and Torre de Belém). It is an official public holiday.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=91" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Romania, 1 May, known as the <b>International Labour Day</b> (<i>Ziua internațională a muncii</i>), the <b>International Workers' Day</b> (<i>Ziua internațională a oamenilor muncii</i>), or simply <b>1/First of May</b> (<i>1/Întâi Mai</i>), is an official <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Romania" title="Public holidays in Romania">public holiday</a>. During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_Romania" title="Communist Romania">communist regime</a>, like in all former Eastern Bloc countries, the day was marked by large state-organised parades in most towns and cities, to which many workers were <i>de facto</i> required to participate. After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanian_Revolution_of_1989" title="Romanian Revolution of 1989">Romanian Revolution of 1989</a>, 1 May continues to be an official public holiday, but without any state organised events or parades. Most people celebrate together with friends and family, organising <a href="/wiki/Picnic" title="Picnic">picnics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbecue" title="Barbecue">barbecues</a>. It is also the first day of the year when people, especially those from the southeastern part of the country including the capital <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>, go to spend the day in one of the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Black_Sea_resorts" title="Romanian Black Sea resorts">Romanian Black Sea resorts</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=92" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%9F-%D0%A0%D0%9F%D0%9A_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%9F-%D0%A0%D0%9F%D0%9A_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg/220px-%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%9F-%D0%A0%D0%9F%D0%9A_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%9F-%D0%A0%D0%9F%D0%9A_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg/330px-%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%9F-%D0%A0%D0%9F%D0%9A_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%9F-%D0%A0%D0%9F%D0%9A_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg/440px-%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%9F-%D0%A0%D0%9F%D0%9A_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%9F-%D0%A0%D0%9F%D0%9A_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Russian Communist Workers' Party demonstration on 1 May 2008 in Izhevsk</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>May Day was celebrated illegally in Russia until the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a> enabled the first legal celebration in 1917. The following year, after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">seizure of power</a>, the May Day celebrations were boycotted by <a href="/wiki/Mensheviks" title="Mensheviks">Mensheviks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Left_Socialist_Revolutionaries" title="Left Socialist Revolutionaries">Left Socialist Revolutionaries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_Russia" title="Anarchism in Russia">anarchists</a>. It became an important official holiday of the Soviet Union, celebrated with elaborate popular parade in the centre of the major cities. The biggest celebration was traditionally organised in <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a>, where the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_CPSU" title="General Secretary of the CPSU">General Secretary of the CPSU</a> and other party and government leaders stood atop <a href="/wiki/Lenin%27s_Mausoleum" title="Lenin's Mausoleum">Lenin's Mausoleum</a> and waved to the crowds. In 1991, which preceded the last year that demonstrations were held in Red Square, May Day grew into high-spirited political action. Around 50,000 people participated in a rally in Red Square in 1991 after which the tradition was interrupted for 13 years. In the early post-Soviet period the holiday turned into massive political gatherings of supporters of radically minded politicians. For instance, an action dubbed as "a rally of communist-oriented organisations" was held in Red Square in 1992. The rally began with performance of the Soviet Union anthem and raising the Red Flag and ended with appeals from the leader of opposition movement Working Moscow, Viktor Anpilov, "for early dismissal of President Boris Yeltsin, ousting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Mayor" title="Moscow Mayor">Moscow Mayor</a> <a href="/wiki/Gavriil_Kharitonovich_Popov" title="Gavriil Kharitonovich Popov">Gavriil Popov</a> from power and putting the latter on trial". Since 1992, May Day is officially called "The Day of Spring and Labour", and remains a major holiday in present-day Russia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=93" title="Edit section: Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Serbia, 1 May (and also 2 May) is a day off work and a day out of school. It is one of the major popular holidays, and the only official holiday from socialist times that is still officially celebrated. People celebrate it all over the country. By tradition 1 May is celebrated by countryside picnics and outdoor barbecues. May is marked by warm weather in Serbia. In <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, the capital, most people go to <a href="/wiki/Avala" title="Avala">Avala</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1utnjak" title="Košutnjak">Košutnjak</a>, which are parks located in Rakovica and Čukarica. People go around the country to enjoy nature. A major religious holiday of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Djurdjevdan" title="Djurdjevdan">Djurdjevdan</a> is on 6 May so quite often days off work are given to connect these two holidays and weekend, creating a small spring break. 1 May is celebrated by most of the population regardless of political views.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovakia">Slovakia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=94" title="Edit section: Slovakia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Slovakia, 1 May is a day off work and a day out of school. Celebrations are usually connected also with the commemoration of the <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">entry of the Slovak Republic into the European Union</a> (1 May 2004).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovenia">Slovenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=95" title="Edit section: Slovenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Slovenia, 1 May (and also 2 May) is a day off work and a day out of school. There are many official celebrations all over the country. In <a href="/wiki/Ljubljana" title="Ljubljana">Ljubljana</a>, the capital, many people go to Rožnik Hill in the city. On the night of 30 April, bonfires are burned on many hills.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG/220px-Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG/330px-Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG/440px-Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May Day rally in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, Spain</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=96" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Spain, the 1 May celebration was established after the death of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Franco</a> in 1975; before that, it had been celebrated during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Second_Republic" title="Spanish Second Republic">Spanish Second Republic</a> period (1931–1939), but it was banned afterwards by the Franco regime. The first time it was celebrated was in 1977, when the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Spain" title="Communist Party of Spain">Communist Party of Spain</a> was legalised. Since then, it has become an official holiday that has been traditionally used by trade unions and leftist parties for social and labour vindications. Commonly, pacific demonstrations and parades occur in major and minor cities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=97" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="918" data-file-width="1236" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg/220px-1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg/330px-1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg/440px-1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Swedish_Social_Democratic_Party" title="Swedish Social Democratic Party">Swedish Social Democratic Party</a> at May Day demonstration in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> in 2006. The party has dominated Swedish politics for nearly a century. The <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Trade_Union_Confederation" title="Swedish Trade Union Confederation">trade union palace</a> in Stockholm is seen at the end of the picture.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>1 May has been an important part of Swedish history since the late 19th century. The day was made a <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">public holiday</a> in 1938 but had been celebrated by the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Social_Democratic_Party" title="Swedish Social Democratic Party">Swedish Social Democratic Party</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V%C3%A4nsterpartiet" title="Vänsterpartiet">left</a> since 1890. The first May Day celebration gathered more than 50,000 people in central Stockholm. The crowd went to hear speeches by the leading figures in the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_labour_movement" title="Swedish labour movement">Swedish labour movement</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Hjalmar_Branting" title="Hjalmar Branting">Hjalmar Branting</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a>), <a href="/wiki/August_Palm" title="August Palm">August Palm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hinke_Bergegren" title="Hinke Bergegren">Hinke Bergegren</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> the demonstrations mainly had a peace message and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_People%27s_Party_(Sweden)" title="Liberal People's Party (Sweden)">Liberal Party</a> also joined the demonstrations. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/8-hour_working_day" title="8-hour working day">8-hour working day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage" title="Women's suffrage">women's suffrage</a> were the principal themes during the troubled times after World War I.</p>
<p>The May Day demonstrations are still an important part of Swedish politics for the social democrats, left-wing parties and unions who use May Day to discuss their politics. In Stockholm the Social Democratic Party always marches towards <a href="/wiki/Norra_Bantorget" title="Norra Bantorget">Norra Bantorget</a>, the centre of the Swedish labour movement, to hold speeches in front of the headquarters of the Swedish Trade Union Confederation, while the smaller <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V%C3%A4nsterpartiet" title="Vänsterpartiet">Left Party</a> marches in larger numbers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup> towards <a href="/wiki/Kungstr%C3%A4dg%C3%A5rden" title="Kungsträdgården">Kungsträdgården</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=98" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Switzerland, the status of 1 May differs depending on the <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland" title="Cantons of Switzerland">canton</a> and sometimes on the municipality. Labour Day is known as <i>Tag der Arbeit</i> in German-speaking cantons, as <i>Fête du Travail</i> in the French-speaking cantons, and as <i>Festa del lavoro</i> in the Italian-speaking canton of Ticino.</p>
<ul>
<li>In the cantons of <a href="/wiki/Basel-Landschaft" title="Basel-Landschaft">Basel-Landschaft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basel-Stadt" title="Basel-Stadt">Basel-Stadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Jura" title="Canton of Jura">Jura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Neuch%C3%A2tel" title="Canton of Neuchâtel">Neuchâtel</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canton_of_Zurich" title="Canton of Zurich">Zürich</a>, Labour Day is an official public holiday equal to Sundays, based on federal law (<i>Bundesgesetz über die Arbeit in Industrie, Gewerbe und Handel</i>, article 20a).</li>
<li>In the cantons of <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Schaffhausen" title="Canton of Schaffhausen">Schaffhausen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thurgau" title="Thurgau">Thurgau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ticino" title="Ticino">Ticino</a>, Labour Day is an official "day off" (<i>Ruhetag</i>). This is equal in practice to an official public holiday, but is not based on federal law and cantonal regulations may differ in details.</li>
<li>In the canton of <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Solothurn" title="Canton of Solothurn">Solothurn</a> it is an official half-day holiday (starting at 12 noon).</li>
<li>In the canton of <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Fribourg" title="Canton of Fribourg">Fribourg</a>, public servants get the afternoon off, many companies follow this practice.</li>
<li>In the canton of <a href="/wiki/Aargau" title="Aargau">Aargau</a> it is not an official holiday, but most employees get the afternoon off.</li>
<li>In the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Hildisrieden" title="Hildisrieden">Hildisrieden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%BCpfheim" title="Schüpfheim">Schüpfheim</a> (both in the canton of <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Lucerne" title="Canton of Lucerne">Lucerne</a>) as well as in <a href="/wiki/Muotathal" title="Muotathal">Muotathal</a> (canton of <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Schwyz" title="Canton of Schwyz">Schwyz</a>), 1 May is an official public holiday, but as commemoration day of the local <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a>, not as Labour Day. In the other parts of the cantons of Lucerne and Schwyz, 1 May is a regular work day.</li>
<li>In all other cantons, 1 May is a regular work day.</li>
</ul>
<p>The largest Labour Day celebrations in Switzerland are held in the city of <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>. Each year, Zürich's 1 May committee, together with the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federation_of_Trade_Unions" title="Swiss Federation of Trade Unions">Swiss Federation of Trade Unions</a>, organises a festival and 1 May rally. It is the largest rally held on a regular basis in Switzerland.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=99" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg/220px-May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg/330px-May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg/440px-May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Istanbul May Day clashes in 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1919" data-file-width="3174" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG/220px-Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG/330px-Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG/440px-Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Workers marching to Taksim Square, 1 May 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>1 May is an official holiday celebrated in Turkey. It was a holiday until 1981 when it was cancelled after the <a href="/wiki/1980_Turkish_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1980 Turkish coup d'état">1980 coup d'état</a>. In 2010, the Turkish government restored the holiday after some casualties and demonstrations. <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square" title="Taksim Square">Taksim Square</a> is the centre of the celebrations due to the <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square_massacre" title="Taksim Square massacre">Taksim Square massacre</a>.</p>
<p>Workers' Day was first celebrated in 1912 in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C4%B0stanbul" title="İstanbul">İstanbul</a>, in 1911 in <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Selânik</a> and in 1899 in <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">İzmir</a>. After the establishment of the Turkish Republic, it became an official holiday. In 1924, it was forbidden by a decree and in both 1924 and 1925, demonstrations were intervened by arm floats. In 1935, The National Assembly declared Workers' Day to be a holiday again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marksist.com_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-marksist.com-61">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the events leading to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1980_Turkish_coup_d%27etat" title="1980 Turkish coup d'etat">1980 Turkish coup d'etat</a>, a massacre occurred on 1 May 1977 (Taksim Square massacre), in which unknown people (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Provocateurs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Provocateurs (page does not exist)">provocateurs</a>) opened fire on the crowd. The crowd was the biggest in Turkish workers' history with the number of people approximating 500,000. In the next two years, provocations and confusion continued and peaked before the 1980 coup d'etat. The Workers' Day holiday was cancelled once again. Still, demonstrations continued with small crowds, and in 1996, three people were killed by police bullets, and a plain-clothes man who spied in the crowd was revealed and lynched by workers. On the same evening, a video broadcast on TV showed that two participants in the demonstration were lynched by far right-wing nationalist groups and this lynching occurred in front of police forces who were watching the scene with happy faces. Thus, 1 May 1996 has been remembered by workers' movements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marksist.com_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-marksist.com-61">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, the 30th anniversary of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taksim_square_massacre" title="Taksim square massacre">Taksim square massacre</a>, leftist workers' unions wanted to commemorate the massacre in Taksim square. Since the government would not let them into the square, 580–700 people were stopped and 1 person died under police control. After these events, the government declared 1 May as "Work and Solidarity Day" but not as a holiday. In the next year, the day was declared as a holiday, but people were still not allowed to gather in Taksim Square.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup> The year 2008 was remembered with police violence in Istanbul. Police fired tear gas grenades among the crowds, and into hospitals and a primary school. Workers pushed forward so that in 2010, 140,000 people gathered in Taksim, and in 2011 there were more than half a million demonstrators.</p>
<p>After 3 years of peaceful meetings in 2013, meetings in <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square" title="Taksim Square">Taksim Square</a> were forbidden by the government. Clashes occurred between police and workers; <a href="/wiki/Water_cannon" title="Water cannon">water cannon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tear_gas" title="Tear gas">tear gas</a> have been widely used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=100" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It is a public holiday in Ukraine, inherited from the Soviet era. <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Ukraine" title="Communist Party of Ukraine">Ukrainian communists</a> and socialists celebrate the holiday with demonstrations, while other people go to picnics and spring vacations.</p>
<p>In 2015, May Day rallies were banned in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv" title="Kharkiv">Kharkiv</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Late May 2015 <a href="/wiki/Decommunization_in_Ukraine" title="Decommunization in Ukraine">laws that ban communist symbols</a> came into effect in Ukraine, thus banning communist symbols, singing the Soviet national hymn or the Internationale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Arsen_Avakov" title="Arsen Avakov">Arsen Avakov</a> during the 2016 May Day rallies in some major cities the number of <a href="/wiki/National_Police_of_Ukraine" title="National Police of Ukraine">police officers</a> far outnumbered the number of rally participants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mptrmd16U_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-mptrmd16U-66">[63]</a></sup> With in <a href="/wiki/Dnipropetrovsk" title="Dnipropetrovsk">Dnipropetrovsk</a> 193 policemen protecting 25 rally participants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mptrmd16U_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-mptrmd16U-66">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=101" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:May_Day_in_London.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/May_Day_in_London.jpg/220px-May_Day_in_London.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/May_Day_in_London.jpg/330px-May_Day_in_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/May_Day_in_London.jpg/440px-May_Day_in_London.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:May_Day_in_London.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Stalin banner belonging to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CPGB-ML" title="CPGB-ML">CPGB-ML</a>, featured in every London International Workers' Day rally since 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>May Day activities (from 1978) are on the first Monday of the month. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> in recent years, the <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalism" title="Anti-capitalism">anti-capitalist</a> movement has organised a number of large protests in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a>. In London, these have resulted in clashes with the police. In 2000, the clashes ended with a branch of <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> being smashed, and a statue of <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> being given a grass <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_hairstyle" title="Mohawk hairstyle">Mohawk hairstyle</a>. The <a href="/wiki/The_Cenotaph,_Whitehall" title="The Cenotaph, Whitehall">Cenotaph</a> was also defaced with <a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">graffiti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[65]</a></sup> In the last few years, demonstrations have been more peaceful, with marches and gatherings, particularly in central London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup> The Conservative-led coalition government in March 2011 announced plans to move the May Day bank holiday to October in order to lengthen the tourist season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MayDayabolishedUK_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-MayDayabolishedUK-70">[67]</a></sup> A London rally on May Day is organised by the London May Day Organising Committee (LMDOC).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=102" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=103" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Labourday1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="488" data-file-width="650" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Labourday1.jpg/220px-Labourday1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Labourday1.jpg/330px-Labourday1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Labourday1.jpg/440px-Labourday1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Labourday1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Labour Day March in Brisbane, Queensland is the largest rally in Australia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While unofficial activities and commemorations associated with International Workers' Day occur on May Day in Australia, <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a> in the various states and territories generally falls on other days. Only in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a> is Labour Day celebrated on the first Monday in May, which is a public holiday under the name of "May Day". <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a> holds the biggest rallies in Australia, with the rally in <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> averaging 30,000 people. There are also rallies held in <a href="/wiki/Cairns" title="Cairns">Cairns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rockhampton" title="Rockhampton">Rockhampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Townsville" title="Townsville">Townsville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcaldine,_Queensland" title="Barcaldine, Queensland">Barcaldine</a> <a href="/wiki/Ipswich,_Queensland" title="Ipswich, Queensland">, Ipswich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toowoomba" title="Toowoomba">Toowoomba</a> and other regional centres.</p>

<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">I saw a man, whom I afterwards identified as Fielding [sic], standing on a truck wagon at the corner of what is known as Crane's Alley. I raised my baton and, in a loud voice, ordered them to disperse as peaceable citizens. I also called upon three persons in the crowd to assist in dispersing the mob. Fielding got down from the wagon, saying at the time, "We are peaceable," as he uttered the last word, I heard a terrible explosion behind where I was standing, followed almost instantly by an irregular volley of pistol shots in our front and from the sidewalk on the east side of the street, which was immediately followed by regular and well directed volleys from the police and which was kept up for several minutes. I then ordered the injured men brought to the stations and sent for surgeons to attend to their injuries. After receiving the necessary attention most of the injured officers were removed to the County Hospital and I highly appreciate the manner in which they were received by Warden McGarrigle who did all in his power to make them comfortable as possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-William_Ward.2C_Capt._3rd_Prect_report_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-William_Ward.2C_Capt._3rd_Prect_report-10">[9]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>5월 1일을 근로자의 날로 하고 이 날을 "근로기준법"에 의한 유급휴일로 한다.</i> ("The first day of May each year shall be designated as Workers' Day, which shall be a paid holiday under the '<a href="/wiki/Labor_Standards_Act" title="Labor Standards Act">Labor Standards Act</a>'.)"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
